If you cannot find ferric acid, use white vinegar and/or strong coffee (it takes longer). Remove the blade from the acid on occasion to judge how deep of an etch is desired, as it may take several minutes. Once the desired level of etch is reached, do not wipe the blade with a rag as this will wipe off the dark oxide layer. Submerge the blade in a mixture of baking soda and warm water or spray it with Windex to neutralize the acid. Dry quickly with compressed air or a hair dryer to prevent flash rusting.<br>\r\n\t<br>\r\n\tCARE INSTRUCTIONS: To preserve the finish of the steel and increase contrast, coat the blade in a light oil (WD-40, Break-Free, etc.), clear paint, or Renaissance Wax. Mix ferric chloride acid with distilled water (1 part water, 2 parts acid), or 60% ferric chloride and 40% white vinegar. Dip blade in a plastic container containing the acid mixture and allow a few minutes for the etching to occur. If you cannot find ferric acid, use white vinegar and/or strong coffee (it takes longer). Remove the blade from the acid on occasion to judge how deep of an etch is desired, as it may take several minutes. Once the desired level of etch is reached, do not wipe the blade with a rag as this will wipe off the dark oxide layer. Submerge the blade in a mixture of baking soda and warm water or spray it with Windex to neutralize the acid. Dry quickly with compressed air or a hair dryer to prevent flash rusting.<br>\r\n\t<br>\r\n\tCARE INSTRUCTIONS: To preserve the finish of the steel and increase contrast, coat the blade in a light oil (WD-40, Break-Free, etc.), clear paint, or Renaissance Wax. If used in the kitchen, Pam or mineral oil works great to prevent rust and is food safe. Turn oven off and allow blade to slowly cool to room temperature. Repeat if a double draw is desired. Blade should be "light straw" in color to reach approximately 58 Rockwell.<br>\r\n\t<br>\r\n\tETCHING PROCESS: Use caution when using acid! Degrease blade with acetone. Mix ferric chloride acid with distilled water (1 part water, 2 parts acid), or 60% ferric chloride and 40% white vinegar. Dip blade in a plastic container containing the acid mixture and allow a few minutes for the etching to occur. If you cannot find ferric acid, use white vinegar and/or strong coffee (it takes longer). Remove the blade from the acid on occasion to judge how deep of an etch is desired, as it may take several minutes. Once the desired level of etch is reached, do not wipe the blade with a rag as this will wipe off the dark oxide layer. Submerge the blade in a mixture of baking soda and warm water or spray it with Windex to neutralize the acid. Dry quickly with compressed air or a hair dryer to prevent flash rusting.<br>\r\n\t<br>\r\n\tCARE INSTRUCTIONS: To preserve the finish of the steel and increase contrast, coat the blade in a light oil (WD-40, Break-Free, etc.), clear paint, or Renaissance Wax. If used in the kitchen, Pam or mineral oil works great to prevent rust and is food safe. After use, like any quality tool, ensure blades are wiped clean, oiled, and kept dry.</span></span></p>\t\t\t</div>', 'manufacturer': 'Alabama Damascus', 'image_urls': ['https://www.knifekits.com/vcom/images/carbon_damascus_8_1_1500.jpg', 'https://www.knifekits.com/vcom/images/sample1_1500.jpg'], 'breadcrumbs': ['Home', 'Catalog', 'Knife Making - Steel', 'USACARBDAM-08']}

Quench in light weight oil.<br>\r\n\t<br>\r\n\tTEMPER OR DRAW: Heat oven up to 350°F and allow blade to stay at this temperature for 1 hour. Turn oven off and allow blade to slowly cool to room temperature. Repeat if a double draw is desired. Blade should be "light straw" in color to reach approximately 58 Rockwell.<br>\r\n\t<br>\r\n\tETCHING PROCESS: Use caution when using acid! Degrease blade with acetone. Mix ferric chloride acid with distilled water (1 part water, 2 parts acid), or 60% ferric chloride and 40% white vinegar. Dip blade in a plastic container containing the acid mixture and allow a few minutes for the etching to occur. If you cannot find ferric acid, use white vinegar and/or strong coffee (it takes longer). Remove the blade from the acid on occasion to judge how deep of an etch is desired, as it may take several minutes. Once the desired level of etch is reached, do not wipe the blade with a rag as this will wipe off the dark oxide layer. Submerge the blade in a mixture of baking soda and warm water or spray it with Windex to neutralize the acid. Dry quickly with compressed air or a hair dryer to prevent flash rusting.<br>\r\n\t<br>\r\n\tCARE INSTRUCTIONS: To preserve the finish of the steel and increase contrast, coat the blade in a light oil (WD-40, Break-Free, etc.), clear paint, or Renaissance Wax. If used in the kitchen, Pam or mineral oil works great to prevent rust and is food safe. After use, like any quality tool, ensure blades are wiped clean, oiled, and kept dry.</span></span></p>\t\t\t</div>', 'manufacturer': 'Alabama Damascus', 'image_urls': ['https://www.knifekits.com/vcom/images/carbon_damascus_12_1_1500.jpg', 'https://www.knifekits.com/vcom/images/sample1-random-ladder_1500.jpg'], 'breadcrumbs': ['Home', 'Catalog', 'Knife Making - Steel', 'USACARBDAM-12']}

Mix ferric chloride acid with distilled water (1 part water, 2 parts acid), or 60% ferric chloride and 40% white vinegar. Dip blade in a plastic container containing the acid mixture and allow a few minutes for the etching to occur. If you cannot find ferric acid, use white vinegar and/or strong coffee (it takes longer). Remove the blade from the acid on occasion to judge how deep of an etch is desired, as it may take several minutes. Once the desired level of etch is reached, do not wipe the blade with a rag as this will wipe off the dark oxide layer. Submerge the blade in a mixture of baking soda and warm water or spray it with Windex to neutralize the acid. Dry quickly with compressed air or a hair dryer to prevent flash rusting.<br>\r\n\t<br>\r\n\tCARE INSTRUCTIONS: To preserve the finish of the steel and increase contrast, coat the blade in a light oil (WD-40, Break-Free, etc.), clear paint, or Renaissance Wax. If used in the kitchen, Pam or mineral oil works great to prevent rust and is food safe. After use, like any quality tool, ensure blades are wiped clean, oiled, and kept dry.</span></span></p>\t\t\t</div>', 'manufacturer': 'Alabama Damascus', 'image_urls': ['https://www.knifekits.com/vcom/images/carbon_damascus_19_1_1500.jpg', 'https://www.knifekits.com/vcom/images/sample1-random_1500.jpg'], 'breadcrumbs': ['Home', 'Catalog', 'Knife Making - Steel', 'USACARBDAM-19']}

Dip blade in a plastic container containing the acid mixture and allow a few minutes for the etching to occur. If you cannot find ferric acid, use white vinegar and/or strong coffee (it takes longer). Remove the blade from the acid on occasion to judge how deep of an etch is desired, as it may take several minutes. Once the desired level of etch is reached, do not wipe the blade with a rag as this will wipe off the dark oxide layer. Submerge the blade in a mixture of baking soda and warm water or spray it with Windex to neutralize the acid. Dry quickly with compressed air or a hair dryer to prevent flash rusting.<br>\r\n\t<br>\r\n\tCARE INSTRUCTIONS: To preserve the finish of the steel and increase contrast, coat the blade in a light oil (WD-40, Break-Free, etc.), clear paint, or Renaissance Wax. Remove the blade from the acid on occasion to judge how deep of an etch is desired, as it may take several minutes. Once the desired level of etch is reached, do not wipe the blade with a rag as this will wipe off the dark oxide layer. Submerge the blade in a mixture of baking soda and warm water or spray it with Windex to neutralize the acid. Dry quickly with compressed air or a hair dryer to prevent flash rusting.<br>\r\n\t<br>\r\n\tCARE INSTRUCTIONS: To preserve the finish of the steel and increase contrast, coat the blade in a light oil (WD-40, Break-Free, etc.), clear paint, or Renaissance Wax. Submerge the blade in a mixture of baking soda and warm water or spray it with Windex to neutralize the acid. Dry quickly with compressed air or a hair dryer to prevent flash rusting.<br>\r\n\t<br>\r\n\tCARE INSTRUCTIONS: To preserve the finish of the steel and increase contrast, coat the blade in a light oil (WD-40, Break-Free, etc.), clear paint, or Renaissance Wax. If used in the kitchen, Pam or mineral oil works great to prevent rust and is food safe. After use, like any quality tool, ensure blades are wiped clean, oiled, and kept dry.</span></span></p>\t\t\t</div>', 'manufacturer': 'Alabama Damascus', 'image_urls': ['https://www.knifekits.com/vcom/images/carbon_damascus_26_1_1500.jpg', 'https://www.knifekits.com/vcom/images/sample1-random-ladder_1500.jpg'], 'breadcrumbs': ['Home', 'Catalog', 'Knife Making - Steel', 'USACARBDAM-26']}

Remove the blade from the acid on occasion to judge how deep of an etch is desired, as it may take several minutes. Once the desired level of etch is reached, do not wipe the blade with a rag as this will wipe off the dark oxide layer. Submerge the blade in a mixture of baking soda and warm water or spray it with Windex to neutralize the acid. Dry quickly with compressed air or a hair dryer to prevent flash rusting.<br>\r\n\t<br>\r\n\tCARE INSTRUCTIONS: To preserve the finish of the steel and increase contrast, coat the blade in a light oil (WD-40, Break-Free, etc.), clear paint, or Renaissance Wax. Once the desired level of etch is reached, do not wipe the blade with a rag as this will wipe off the dark oxide layer. Submerge the blade in a mixture of baking soda and warm water or spray it with Windex to neutralize the acid. Dry quickly with compressed air or a hair dryer to prevent flash rusting.<br>\r\n\t<br>\r\n\tCARE INSTRUCTIONS: To preserve the finish of the steel and increase contrast, coat the blade in a light oil (WD-40, Break-Free, etc.), clear paint, or Renaissance Wax. If used in the kitchen, Pam or mineral oil works great to prevent rust and is food safe. After use, like any quality tool, ensure blades are wiped clean, oiled, and kept dry.</span></span></p>\t\t\t</div>', 'manufacturer': 'Alabama Damascus', 'image_urls': ['https://www.knifekits.com/vcom/images/carbon_damascus_8_1_1500.jpg', 'https://www.knifekits.com/vcom/images/sample1_1500.jpg'], 'breadcrumbs': ['Home', 'Catalog', 'Knife Making - Steel', 'USACARBDAM-08']}

If you cannot find ferric acid, use white vinegar and/or strong coffee (it takes longer). Remove the blade from the acid on occasion to judge how deep of an etch is desired, as it may take several minutes. Once the desired level of etch is reached, do not wipe the blade with a rag as this will wipe off the dark oxide layer. Submerge the blade in a mixture of baking soda and warm water or spray it with Windex to neutralize the acid. Dry quickly with compressed air or a hair dryer to prevent flash rusting.<br>\r\n\t<br>\r\n\tCARE INSTRUCTIONS: To preserve the finish of the steel and increase contrast, coat the blade in a light oil (WD-40, Break-Free, etc.), clear paint, or Renaissance Wax.
